1935.10.20

Dawn of Peace: France Agrees to Aid Britain's Navy; Britain and Italy to Issue Statement Soon; British Mediterranean Fleet May Be Reduced; Italy Said to Have Proposed Armistice Terms 1

(Paris) As a result of improved talks between the British, French, and Italian representatives in Rome, the prospects for peace have suddenly brightened today. It is further announced that Britain and Italy will soon issue an important joint statement, further increasing the optimistic atmosphere. Diplomats today believe that this may gradually lead to a path of reconciliation in the Italo-Abyssinian conflict. (October 18, National Telegram)

(Paris) It was formally announced here today that French Premier Laval has definitively replied to Britain, stating that if Italian forces attack the British Navy in the Mediterranean, France is determined to cooperate with Britain. According to a report from the British Ambassador, Laval has fully satisfied Britain's inquiry regarding whether France will assist Britain in the future. (October 18, National Telegram)

(Rome) As a result of repeated diplomatic negotiations, Britain has agreed today to withdraw a portion of its fleet from the Mediterranean. Mussolini has also agreed to reduce the troops concentrated in Libya. France has agreed to send warships to fill the defensive duties vacated by the withdrawing British ships in the Mediterranean. This agreement was reached today by the British Ambassador to Italy, Drummond, in separate meetings with Mussolini and the French Ambassador to Italy, de Chambrun. It is stipulated that the French Navy will sail to the Mediterranean, protecting British interests when necessary. According to Italian sources today, there is hope for a peaceful resolution of the current tense situation. A statement issued by the Foreign Ministry states that the continued talks between the British, French, and Italian representatives indicate that the doors to reconciliation have not been closed in the dispute threatening Europe. (October 18, National Telegram)

(Rome) Discussions are currently underway in Rome and Paris, and opinions are being exchanged between London and Paris, raising hopes that a peace movement is being launched again. The British Ambassador to Italy, Drummond, met with Italian Premier Mussolini this morning, and the French Ambassador to Italy met with Mussolini on Tuesday. French Premier Laval received the Italian Ambassador in Paris today. According to reliable sources here, talks are being conducted through diplomatic channels between Paris and Rome, and between Paris and London. The exact details are not yet known, but the fact that talks are continuing proves that the doors have not been closed. (October 18, Reuters)

(Paris) The outline of France's reply was conveyed this morning by Premier Laval to the British Ambassador to France, Sir Clerk. The full text will be formally delivered to the British government tonight.

According to a spokesman for the French Foreign Ministry, rumors of disagreements between Britain and France are due to inaccurate interpretations by the newspapers of both countries regarding the views of their respective governments. As far as France is concerned, France is prepared to fulfill the mutual assistance obligations under Article 16, Paragraph 3 of the League of Nations Covenant. France is willing to assume its share of collective responsibility and will not shirk it. However, given the current situation, France believes that it is not yet necessary to implement the provisions of Article 16, Paragraph 3 of the Covenant. This is France's intention, and there is no other. It is hoped that British cabinet members will make a clear statement so that the tense situation created by the newspapers' advocacy can be eased.

Italian Ambassador to France Cerruti met with Laval this morning and presented Italy's conditions for stopping the war against Abyssinia and the basis for resolving the dispute. However, officials are unwilling to disclose the details of the conversation, stating only that Cerruti's remarks were of a reporting nature. (October 18, Havas)

(London) Britain recently inquired of France whether France would be willing to assist Britain if the British fleet in the Mediterranean were attacked by Italy. France has replied in the affirmative, and the reply was delivered last night to Sir Clerk, the British Ambassador in Paris. According to responsible sources in Paris, the reply has dispelled misunderstandings between Britain and France. France is prepared to fulfill its obligation under Article 16, Section 3 of the League of Nations Covenant to provide mutual assistance in the event of danger arising from the imposition of sanctions. London was very pleased with this reply. Political circles believe that France has given a satisfactory answer to what Britain considers a necessary point of cooperation between Britain and France in Geneva. It is reported that Britain is now willing to consider withdrawing some of the excess tonnage concentrated in the Mediterranean, but two conditions must be met before the British fleet in the Mediterranean is reduced to its normal strength: (1) Italy must withdraw the troops it has increased in Libya; (2) There must be a perceptible improvement in the overall situation. This refers to the cessation of Italian newspapers' attacks on Britain. Although this condition may be fulfilled in the future, there is currently no understanding between the British and Italian governments. (October 19, Reuters)

(London) Political circles in London today confirmed that the British fleet in the Mediterranean will not be reduced to its normal strength at this time. Britain will only take this step after Italy reduces its troops stationed in Libya and Italian newspapers stop attacking Britain. However, Britain and Italy are currently engaged in talks in Rome, and if results are achieved, a joint communiqué will be issued. Then, these two conditions may be fulfilled by Italy. France has stated that it is willing to assist Britain if Italy attacks the British fleet in the Mediterranean. Britain may announce the withdrawal of two battleships from Gibraltar in return. The document from France to Britain on this matter will not be published. The main idea is to explain that France's diplomatic policy in the Italo-Abyssinian dispute is very open and aboveboard. (October 19, Reuters)

(Rome) Premier Mussolini had an important conversation with British Ambassador Drummond yesterday. The results will be announced before noon on Sunday. The purpose of this conversation is to clear the air between Britain and Italy. It is now believed that although the tension between Britain and Italy may not be completely dispelled, there is no risk of either side acting rashly. Since the concentration of British warships in the Mediterranean, it has been generally believed that this is a sign of Britain taking military sanctions, or at least wanting to blockade Italian ports. (October 18, Havas)

(London) According to official sources, the British government is planning to recall the warships HMS Holt and HMS Renown from the Strait of Gibraltar in the near future. Regarding the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, news has been received here from Rome stating that the negotiations between Italian Premier Mussolini and the Emperor of Abyssinia are progressing well. However, powerful sources here believe that the demands made by the Italian government may not be accepted by Britain, as these demands are excessive. (October 19, Havas)

Boycott of Italian Goods by Various Countries Begins October 31st: Decision by the Committee of Eighteen Nations 2

(Geneva) The Committee of Eighteen Nations decided today to implement a boycott of all Italian goods starting October 31st. The General Committee of 52 Nations will meet this afternoon and is expected to approve it. The League of Nations' sanctions against Italy are thus moving forward on three fronts: (1) An arms embargo against Italy has been implemented by 16 countries; (2) A severance of financial relations with Italy has been implemented by countries such as Soviet Russia, Latvia, and Finland; (3) A boycott of Italian goods will be implemented at the end of the month. (October 19, National Telegram)

(Geneva) Fourteen countries have now notified the League of Nations that they are willing to lift the ban on arms exports to Abyssinia while simultaneously prohibiting the supply of arms to Italy. The latest reports of compliance come from Sweden, Uruguay, Lithuania, and the Irish Free State. (October 19, Reuters)

Page 4

League of Nations Sanctions Against Italy: Ministry of Foreign Affairs Receives Official Notification; Implementation Methods and Scope Being Studied in Detail by Central Government 3

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, after the League of Nations passed economic sanctions against Italy, it notified all member states via broadcast from Geneva. The official text is being mailed and has not yet arrived in Nanjing. The government is studying in detail the methods and scope of implementing the sanctions. It is generally observed that China's attitude must both fulfill its obligations as a member state and take into account its own special circumstances. (October 19, Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After China received notification of the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy, the methods and scope of their implementation are being studied in detail. On the one hand, it is necessary to fulfill the obligations of a member state, and on the other hand, it is necessary to consider China's special circumstances. (October 19, Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) The Coordinating Committee established by the League of Nations under Article 16 of the Covenant made two recommendations on October 16th. The Secretary-General of the League of Nations notified the governments of member states. Our Ministry of Foreign Affairs has also received its official notification. In addition to translating it and submitting it to the Executive Yuan for review, the full translated text of its telegram is extracted as follows:

The Secretary-General of the League of Nations, on behalf of the Coordinating Committee established under Article 16 of the Covenant, transmits to the governments of member states the original proposal announced at the committee meeting on October 16th. The Coordinating Committee's resolution believes that the measures that the committee has proposed and will continue to propose must be implemented quickly and effectively. While it is understood that each country must implement these measures in accordance with its own laws and in accordance with its government's power to implement treaties, the fact that must be noted is that member states of the League of Nations must abide by the obligations arising from Article 16 of the Covenant and take the necessary steps to fulfill their obligations with the necessary speed.

Recommendation 1: The revised table reviewed by the Small Committee of Experts is attached to replace the attached table to the first recommendation. The items considered are arms and ammunition. Category 1: (1) Rifles and pistols and their barrels; (2) Machine guns, automatic rifles, submachine guns of various calibers and barrel lengths; (3) Guns, short cannons, and cannons of various calibers, as well as their matching pipes and rotating parts; (4) Ammunition used in the military equipment listed in items 1 and 2 above, empty shells and codes used in the military equipment listed in item 3, and the charging of these military equipment; (5) Empty grenades, bombs, torpedoes, mines, and their launching equipment; (6) Tank vehicles, armored transporters, armored trains, and all armored products. Category 2: All kinds of warships, including aircraft carriers and submarines (Note: Aviation terminology is based on the Aviation Terminology Dictionary compiled by the Central Aviation School). Category 3 (combining categories 3 and 5 in the Coordinating Committee's documents): (1) Armored and disassembled aircraft, including those heavier than air and lighter than air, and their propellers or air propellers, high-altitude gun mounts or guns, and fuselage tail assembly landing gear assembly; (2) Aircraft engines. Category 4: Pistols and automatic pistols exceeding one pound and six taels in weight (630 grams). Category 5: (1) Incendiary bombs and all other projectiles used in chemical or incendiary warfare; (2) Tear gas, methyl arsenic dioxide, ethyl arsenic dichloride, and other toxic agents used for chemical or incendiary warfare; (3) Powders used for combat and explosion. When adopting the above text, the Chairman made the following statement: Regarding the items in Category 5, Item 2, according to the 1925 Convention, their use has already been prohibited and is still prohibited. They are mentioned again because their uses are becoming more widespread, leading to even less restriction on their manufacture. The Committee solemnly declares that these various products must absolutely not be transported to Italy. The original text of the first recommendation is further mentioned as follows: For the convenience of member states in complying with the obligations of Article 16 of the Covenant, the following measures shall be implemented immediately: 1. Member states that have prohibited or restricted the export, transit, or passage of arms and ammunition to Abyssinia shall abolish such measures immediately. 2. The governments of member states of the League of Nations shall immediately prohibit the export, transit, or passage of the arms and ammunition listed in the attached table to Italy or its territories. 3. The governments of member states of the League of Nations shall take the necessary steps to ensure that the arms and ammunition listed in the attached table that are transported to countries other than Italy are not directly or indirectly transported to Italy or its territories. 4. The measures stipulated in Items 2 and 3 shall apply to contracts that are currently being fulfilled, and all governments are requested to inform the Secretary-General of the Committee as soon as possible of how they are implementing all of the above measures for transmission to the Committee.

Recommendation 2: For the convenience of member states of the League of Nations in fulfilling their obligations under Article 16 of the Covenant, the following measures must be adopted immediately. Member states of the League of Nations must immediately adopt the necessary measures to prevent the following events from occurring: (1) The granting of loans to the Italian government and the raising of loans in Italy and elsewhere on behalf of the national government; (2) The granting of bank loans and other loans to the Italian government, the continued granting of subsidies to the Italian government, or other continued overdrafts, as well as the lending of loans directly or indirectly to the Italian government in accordance with valid contracts; (3) The granting of all loans to government offices or companies within Italy, and the raising of funds for these loans in Italy or elsewhere; (4) The granting of various bank loans or other loans to any government office or company within Italy, the continued granting of subsidies to any government office or company within Italy, or the allowing of continued overdrafts, as well as the lending of loans directly or indirectly to the government office or society; (5) The issuance of various stocks or the raising of other funds on behalf of any government office or company within Italy, as well as the issuance of such stocks or the raising of funds in Italy or elsewhere; (6) Governments must take all necessary steps to ensure that the matters in the aforementioned items 1 to 5 do not take effect directly or through any person of any nationality. Governments are requested to implement these proposed measures immediately without the need for legislative procedures and to fully implement these measures with all implementing steps by October 31, 1935. Governments that cannot obtain the necessary legislative procedures in this way are requested to notify the Secretary-General of the League of Nations of the expected date of implementation for transmission to the Committee. Furthermore, all governments are requested to notify the Secretary-General of the League of Nations as soon as possible of the measures they have followed in accordance with the aforementioned provisions for transmission to the Committee. At the end of the second recommendation, it is expressed that it is hoped that all governments will notify the Secretary-General of the League of Nations as soon as possible of the measures they have followed in accordance with this recommendation for transmission to the Committee. For the convenience of the Committee, it is best for each government to submit the original text of the laws, orders, proclamations, or other official documents that include or implement the above measures, and to translate the gist into English or French and send it to the Coordinating Committee along with the original text. The following text is also adopted: For the benefit of member states of the League of Nations in fulfilling their obligations under Article 16 of the Covenant, any recommendations for action in accordance with Article 16 are based on the following provisions of the article: Member states of the League of Nations agree to mutually assist in financial and economic measures to resist any special measures implemented by a country that violates the Covenant against any member. The above text is a reiteration of the notification of October 14. When the aforementioned recommendations were adopted, the Chairman announced that these measures do not apply to charitable donations or payments to religious organizations, which are also clearly agreed to be in this category. (October 19, Central News Agency)

Chaotic Eastern African War News: Italian Forces Consolidate Newly Occupied Positions; Abyssinian Forces Said to Be Counter-Attacking 4

(Rome) Italian forces on the northern front are currently consolidating their positions and are using thousands of personnel to build roads behind the front lines and construct five large reservoirs. Once the project is completed, they will attack Magal. There were no serious battles on the southern front today. However, several Italian aircraft reconnoitered the area 20 miles southeast of Jijiga, southeast of the Djibouti-Addis Ababa railway. This is the closest point to the key city of Harar that Italian aircraft have approached. (October 19, Reuters)

Addis Ababa According to a communiqué, Italian aircraft bombed the town of Magal, 65 miles southeast of Adowa, today and strafed the area with machine guns, killing and wounding 60 Abyssinian soldiers. At the same time, thousands of Italian workers, protected by aircraft, are working day and night to expand roads and water sources in order to attack Magal. This is the second largest objective of the Italian forces on the northern front. According to reliable sources, Italian forces are currently advancing along the Surra River, and their vanguard has reached a location near Adamiso, 20 miles from Magal, without encountering Abyssinian resistance. However, they have suffered casualties from Abyssinian sniper fire. It is not yet known whether the Abyssinian forces intend to defend Magal. However, the town is located on a mountain, and the hillside slopes northward, so it may not be as easy for the Italian forces to capture as Adowa. If the Italian forces capture Magal, it will take a long time to build defensive works, as the terrain to the southwest and south is very difficult to travel. The malaria-ridden Takazze Desert is a natural barrier to proceeding to Lake Tana, and the mountain range south of Magal is a commercial route where Abyssinian guerrillas can take advantage of the terrain to inflict heavy damage on the enemy. (October 18, Reuters)

(London) It is reported from here that mysterious and significant military changes have occurred on the southeastern front in Abyssinia. It is reported that Italian forces are rapidly advancing into the plains, intending to cut the Djibouti-Addis Ababa railway. However, official reports state that heavy rains have hampered the progress of the Italian forces, which was unexpected. According to reliable sources, the plan of Italian Commander Graziani to attack the railway with a large number of high-speed small tanks has encountered unexpected obstacles. It is also reported that Abyssinian Southeastern Front Commander Nasibu has now concentrated a large army to protect the railway. (October 18, National Telegram)

Mogadishu, Italian Somaliland Torrential rains have greatly affected military operations on the Somali front. The attack on Gorahai has been hampered. Rainfall is forecast for another week in the Fafan River area. Rainfall is relatively light in the Shibeli River area, allowing Italian forces to continue their slow advance. (October 18, National Telegram)

Addis Ababa Several warriors from the Uollamo tribe of Abyssinia, known for their strength and indomitable spirit, are currently stationed on the outskirts of Addis Ababa, awaiting orders to go to the front. Today, they staged a demonstration outside the Italian legation and fired shots without permission. The police were unable to stop them. A team of Abyssinian royal guards rushed to suppress them and arrested several people before dispersing the demonstrators. The Abyssinian king heard about it and immediately ordered that the ringleaders be flogged 25 times each. (October 18, Reuters)

Harar Abyssinian Southeastern Front Commander General Nasibu stated today that the Italian forces will launch a major offensive after resting in the low-lying areas in the south. This heavy rain is an abnormal phenomenon this year. (October 18, National Telegram)

Addis Ababa Our correspondent Ognah reports that the Abyssinian government issued a communiqué stating, "The propaganda from the enemy side that the troops in Guji Province have rebelled is not only completely unfounded, but the troops in that province are currently commanded by Prince Emir and are heading towards the northern front. The Italian forces will soon have the opportunity to test the morale of our army." The communiqué also stated, "More and more Italian soldiers are deserting. The deserters have reported to the Abyssinian army about the Italian forces' preparations for battle, stating that the Italian forces are digging trenches and deploying barbed wire on the Adowa, Aksum, and Adigrat fronts to prevent Abyssinian counter-attacks." As for the general atmosphere in the capital, there has been no change since the start of the war. However, national emotions are extremely intense. The people are making war preparations and are eagerly awaiting the Abyssinian emperor's order to go to war. The general public believes that the Abyssinian army will soon be victorious. (October 19, Havas)

Djibouti A telegram from Addis Ababa states that 500,000 Abyssinian troops are preparing to counter-attack Adowa. (October 18, National Telegram)

France's Reply to Britain 5

(Paris) Regarding France providing assistance when the British Navy is attacked by Italy in the Mediterranean, the reply submitted by the French government was delivered to the British government last night. The contents are divided into two parts. The first part is based on legal principles, roughly stating that France and Britain completely agree on the interpretation of Article 16, Paragraph 3 of the League of Nations Covenant, believing that if a country is attacked by a sanctioned country as a result of implementing the sanctions determined by the League of Nations, all member states of the League of Nations should automatically come to its aid. As far as the current incident is concerned, if a country is attacked by Italy, France and all member states of the League of Nations should come to its aid. However, if this attack by Italy is due to the attacked country acting alone, then Article 16, Paragraph 1 of the Covenant should be invoked and recognized as a new act of aggression. The second part is based on political principles, roughly stating that since the British and Italian governments are unwilling to resort to force and have reiterated that they have no intention of resorting to force, the French government believes that Article 16, Paragraph 3 of the Covenant does not need to be invoked. Furthermore, the sanctions determined by the League of Nations are economic and financial in nature. Italian Premier Mussolini has already stated that he accepts them, so there should be no disputes. In addition, the French government hopes that Britain can withdraw a portion of its fleet stationed in the Mediterranean so that the dispute can be resolved in a friendly manner and possible incidents can be avoided. (October 19, Havas)

Naval Conference Expected to Be Held This Year: All Parties Willing to Participate 6

(London) Hopes are now quite good that a naval conference will be held in London this year. Japan notified the British Foreign Office today, stating that while Japan still insists on its views regarding naval limitations, it is prepared to join the conference. All other naval powers that signed the London and Washington Conventions have now expressed their willingness to participate in the conference. (October 19, Reuters)

(London) Regarding the preliminary talks for the naval conference, the British government made some suggestions to the countries concerned. According to our reporter, the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in Britain, Fujii, delivered his government's reply to the British Foreign Office yesterday afternoon, stating that it was willing to participate in the preliminary talks, but still insisted on the country's basic position, namely that the total tonnage of each country's navy should be relatively equal. This seems to say that although Japan can discuss qualitative restrictions, it demands that its right to equal total naval tonnage be recognized in some way. Thus, although Japan is prepared to participate in the preliminary naval talks, it has not yet been decided whether it will participate in the naval conference in the future. (October 19, Havas)

(Washington) Japanese Ambassador to the United States Saito submitted a memorandum to the State Department today, explaining Japan's views on the naval issue, stating that Japan's attitude towards the international situation has not changed, but it has not closed the door to negotiations. This is the same as the memorandum submitted by the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in Britain to the British Foreign Office. (October 18, National Telegram)

Current Commentary

Farewell to the National Games Athletes 9

— Bing

The grand Sixth National Games, lasting for eleven days, concludes today. The participating athletes have displayed vibrant spirits, promoting and vigorously striving, creating numerous new records. Today, they bid farewell to their companions and return to their hometowns. Those who return with accolades are, of course, pleased with the fame they have rightfully earned. Even those who did not win medals are content with the contributions they have made. The enthusiastic expectations of the vast audience and the unanimous encouragement from newspapers and magazines will undoubtedly leave a deep and pleasant impression, a lifelong memory. However, when these gentlemen leave the sports field and return to their respective hometowns, is this all they take with them?

These gentlemen come from all over the country, even from the remote regions of northern and western China, undeterred by the hardship of travel, eagerly rushing here. Moreover, overseas Chinese compatriots have come in groups, like travelers longing for their homeland. However, the places from which these gentlemen come rarely present a scene of happiness; instead, they are filled with anxieties and troubles. Perhaps a powerful neighbor is extending its claws, poised to seize them. Or perhaps a devastating disaster rages, leaving the people as starving corpses. Or perhaps fields and gardens are abandoned, with farmers lacking the capital to cultivate them. Or perhaps markets and shops are desolate, with merchants at their wits' end regarding their skills in trading and relocating. When these gentlemen mustered their spirits to prepare for this display of skill, they must have simultaneously remembered these various situations, filled with sorrow and lamentation. How could they forget them? Furthermore, the sports field where these gentlemen leaped and ran is located beside an area that was a battlefield just three years ago. During their leisure time, as these gentlemen wandered among the fields, they must have thought of how this land, now covered with crops, was once soaked with the hot blood of those who died for their country. Moreover, they saw broken tiles and ruined walls, charred beams and shattered pillars, imagining the tragic scene of countless lives and properties turned to dust. The feelings that arose in them must have been more than just sighs and lamentations. As these gentlemen shared their homesickness and mourned the traces of war, they must have increased their understanding of the current state of our nation and strengthened their resolve to dedicate themselves to its future. They must have realized that unless they gather the strength of the masses into a great force and unite the hearts of the masses into a great heart, there is no way to save the nation from ruin or ensure its survival in this world. They must also have recognized that this assembly, gathering comrades from various places in one place, is nothing less than a sign of the great force and great heart being solidified. If so, then these gentlemen's departure today represents a breakthrough in their awareness. This is the best harvest of this trip.

These gentlemen possess strong physiques and exceptional skills, which are, of course, gratifying aspects of life. However, the reason they are gratifying is that they provide the means to undertake arduous tasks and serve the masses. As for fame, it is an external thing. Even if it is said that it is by no means accidental, there is no need to let it consume your mind. There are those who excessively praise the sporting cause, calling out the names of the athletes, praising and singing their praises, as if they were circus performers with huge elephants and fierce lions, exclaiming, "How magnificent! How heroic!" Such praise is incessant, but the elephants and lions remain mere playthings. Is this the fame of athletes, or is it actually their shame? On this point, you gentlemen should be especially discerning and handle it well. We also see some who are fond of sports, forgetting that it is a means rather than an end, having no other concerns beyond leaping and running, no other worries beyond defeating opponents and winning. They enjoy it tirelessly, as if it were their lifelong pursuit. This is to betray their great advantage. Even in prosperous and powerful countries, this is not appropriate. How much less so in our weak and troubled nation? How can you boast about this? You gentlemen have been inspired by observing power, and your consciousness has already made a breakthrough. You will probably not fall into this error, will you? A strong physique must be accompanied by correct knowledge. Heroic strength must be applied to practical paths. This is what we expect from you gentlemen, and it is also what you should strive for yourselves. You gentlemen are returning. The autumn wind is already fierce. Please take care of yourselves.

Mongolian Political Council Holds Meetings for Several Consecutive Days; Opening Speech by Prince De 18

Bailingmiao: The Third Plenary Session of the Mongolian Political Council opened on the 9th. More than 200 committee members, princes, and guests arrived. Prince De delivered an opening speech, which briefly stated that the Mongolian Political Council has been formally established for one year. Today is the opening day of the Third Plenary Session of the Mongolian Political Council, which is also the second anniversary of the Mongolian autonomy movement. In these two years, some Chinese have sympathized with us, while others have doubted us. Those who sympathize with us believe that our autonomy is in accordance with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, realizing equality among all ethnic groups in the country, and seeking the survival of the entire Chinese nation. Those who doubt us believe that our autonomy is to break away from the central government and declare independence. Some even mistakenly believe that we have imperialist backing. Reviewing our two-year history, whether we have obeyed the central government or betrayed the central government is clear and undeniable. In short, Mongolian autonomy, politically speaking, is to promote the efficiency of central administration and save the central government from the suffering of being too far away to be effective. Diplomatically speaking, it is to promote good neighborliness and security. In terms of national defense, it is to consolidate border defense. Financially speaking, it is to develop resources. In the future, we will continue to adhere to our original intention, regardless of praise or blame, regardless of success or failure, knowing only that we must take the interests of the nation and the country as the premise, seek the survival of the entire Chinese nation, and be one with the country. We will never destroy the history of our ancestors and bring shame on future generations. O descendants of Genghis Khan, be alert! O descendants of the Yellow race, know this! We only hope for the central government's understanding and the people's analysis. As for the Western Banner incident, it is not worth mentioning. The League Chief under the guidance of our Mongolian Political Council has the power to appoint and remove illegal princes. This customary law has been in place from the Yuan Dynasty to the Republic of China. With this spirit of fairness, we maintain hereditary succession. The governance of our Mongolian Political Council over the banners is the same as the governance of county governments by local provincial governments. (Omitted) Mencius said, "Without rules, there can be no squares and circles." I cannot help but feel deeply moved. I sincerely hope that the central government will give this its final thought. This is what we deeply pray for. At the beginning of this Third Plenary Session, I especially hope that all committee members will have practical proposals to enrich the spirit of autonomy, so as not to fail the high hopes of the people and the cultivation of the central government. From 10:00 am until 1:00 pm, preparatory meetings were held for several consecutive days. On the 15th, Prince Yun arrived at the meeting despite his illness. (Tianjin) The 2nd Security Team of the Funing Security Forces cracked down on a secret gun-making organization in Laomumiao Gou, a village under the jurisdiction of Chengdong Temple, and seized eight gun-making machines manufactured by the Northeast Arsenal and many firearms. The main culprit and Peng Qingxiang and the workers all escaped. The gun-making organization is related to Bai Jianwu. Most of the guns and ammunition used by various bandits on the Great Wall line were supplied by this organization. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Ministry of Finance Cracks Down on Banks' Excessive Deposit-Taking 26

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance believes that the capital of a few privately-run banks is insufficient. They often use high interest rates and gifts as bait to attract deposits and set up excessive branch offices to absorb cash from the interior. Once they go bankrupt and are liquidated, difficulties arise. All the banks that have gone bankrupt in the past year have had this phenomenon. Measures have now been formulated to crack down on the excessive deposit-taking, and orders have been issued to the provincial and municipal governments and the Banking Association on the 19th to strictly investigate and crack down on this. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Jiang Dingwen Arrives in Jiangshan to Meet with Wei Lihuang 27

(Hangzhou) Jiang Dingwen arrived in Jiangshan from Pucheng on the 18th to meet with Wei Lihuang to discuss the suppression of the remaining bandits in southern Zhejiang and northern Fujian. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

(Fuzhou) After Jiang Dingwen and Wei Lihuang finalized the plan to suppress bandits on the border of Zhejiang, Fujian, and Jiangxi in Pucheng, Wei immediately set off to inspect the front line. Jiang will return to Zhang via the province within days. The three or four Sui districts have decided to jointly suppress the bandits led by An Yongde, Zhang Xiong, and Nan. Xie's brigade of the Ninth Division and the Ninth Regiment of the Security Forces are now gathered on the border of De, actively deploying. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

(Xiamen) The four-pronged attack by the Ninth Division on the bandit Zhang Xiongnan in Dehua captured the bandit's nest in Xishan on the evening of the 17th. Zhang's troops were broken up and scattered in all directions. Zhang had more than 2,000 guns and more than ten artillery pieces previously owned by Chen Guohui of Xinde, but all the strategic locations were lost. The Ninth Division is now conducting a zonal suppression of the remaining bandits, searching for hidden weapons. Many of Zhang's key leaders have been captured, making it easy to pacify the area. Zhang is still in Taiwan and has not returned to De. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Guangdong Drafting Measures to Severely Punish Smugglers 28

(Hong Kong) Guangdong is drafting measures to severely punish smugglers. Those who collude with foreigners to smuggle goods, endangering the Republic of China, will be punished with the death penalty. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Inmates Break Out of Prison in Putian 29

(Xiamen) More than 100 inmates of the Putian Fu Yuan Prison revolted during the release period on the afternoon of the 16th, seized the guards' keys, opened the doors, and escaped. The guards had only two guns, one of which was broken, and one shot was obstructed and could not be stopped. 61 people escaped. When the stationed army arrived, they chased back 19 people, and 42 people escaped. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Shuyang Determines Project to Build Flood Prevention Dike; Urban and Rural Towns Have Been Fully Mobilized; Statistics on Losses from the Jun Tun River Breach 30

(Xuzhou) Because the flood from the breaches of various rivers in Shuyang was too great, a 10,000-meter flood prevention dike was specially built. The project has been determined, and the urban and rural towns have been fully mobilized and set off. The largest breach of the Jun Tun River, Huangying Township, flooded more than ten villages and more than 600 households, flooding 140 hectares of farmland. Tunhe Township flooded more than 30 villages and more than 1,000 households, flooding 350 hectares of farmland. The disaster at other breach sites was also serious. Donghai is assisting in handling the flood prevention project in Shuyang. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

(Xuzhou) The Xiaoshishi Bridge near Hongkou Nian, three miles west of Guanyun City, was washed away by the water, and the Yanhe River water flowed directly into Banpu. Thanks to the desperate efforts of the people in one district, they blocked it. Banpu was fortunately not hit by the disaster. They are now encircling the area with levees for defense to prevent flooding. The water level in the Xinpu Yanhe River is currently stable, but communication with the outside world has been mostly cut off since the flood disaster, resulting in high prices and difficult lives for the common people. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Jiang Cables Various Provinces Along the Yangtze River, Instructing Them on Dam Closure Projects 31

(Hankou) Jiang cabled the provinces along the Yangtze River, instructing them on dam closure projects, saying that dam closure projects are not easy. If they do not consider the water situation and act rashly, they may be counterproductive, wasting manpower and materials. They should survey the terrain in advance, determine the plan in detail, prepare materials, and recruit labor, and then carry out construction by assessing the situation. This will save labor and materials and achieve results. (Special Dispatch, 19th)

Ministry of Industries Establishes Niter Refining Plant in Kaifeng 44

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industries believes that the niter and potassium sulfate needed by China's new industries have always been imported. Now, a niter refining plant is established in Kaifeng to purchase crude niter and refine fine niter with a potassium sulfate content of 99%. A potassium sulfate pilot plant will also be established in Henan Province. In the future, distribution agencies will be established in various places. It is found that niter and potassium sulfate are the main ingredients for making leather dyes and glues. China imports about four to five million yuan annually, mostly from Chile. (19th Special Dispatch)

China Industrial Bank to End Lottery Savings at the End of the Year 45

Gao Tingzi Discusses Inspection of Navigation Administration in Various Regions 48

(Nanjing) Gao Tingzi, Director of the Navigation Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, returned to Nanjing after inspecting navigation administration in Shantou, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, Xiamen, Wenzhou, Haimen, Ningbo, Zhenhai and other places. According to him, there has been progress in navigation administration in various places, especially in Guangzhou, Shantou and Ningbo, Zhejiang. The four new ships "Yuan Heng Li Zhen" of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CSSNC) operating in South China have improved their equipment and organization. The Ministry of Communications also ordered CSSNC to improve the equipment of the "Xin Jiang Tian" ship operating between Shanghai and Ningbo, and after the trial use of trained crew members, the bad habits have been eliminated. He traveled from Ningbo to Shanghai on this ship. Regarding the Shantou CSSNC registration incident raised by the Hong Kong government, the ministry will ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to study it and then conduct negotiations. His trip was only a factual investigation. The Ministry of Communications is determined to continuously improve the national navigation administration, aiming to develop the shipping industry, starting with improving equipment. All valley line ships will try their best to add new ships. Secondly, the comprador system will be abolished to avoid bad practices such as tea servants extorting tips. On the one hand, tea servants on each ship will be given considerable training, and those who do not meet the requirements will be eliminated. Since Shanghai has sent personnel to train them under the New Life Movement, significant results have been seen. This training will be completed in one year. In the future, the shipping routes will be expanded, but there are no plans for expansion at this time. While in Shanghai, he met with Liu Hongsheng, Ye Zuotang and others, and they did not re-mention their resignations, so it is hoped that they will withdraw their intentions to resign. (19th Special Dispatch)

Foreigners Collecting Specimens in China Must Comply with Cooperation Regulations 49

(Nanjing) American ornithologist Ke Jeren plans to collect bird skins in Fujian and transport them for scientific research. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs requested the Academia Sinica to handle it. International Commercial Telegraph

October 19th Reuters Exclusive Commercial News 69

Gold and Silver

British Gold: Today's gold price rose by four pence, the price being one hundred and forty-one shillings and seven and a half pence.

British Silver: Large spot silver remains at twenty-nine pence three one two five, but forward silver rose by point zero six two five to twenty-nine pence three one two five. China, the United States and India are all engaged in buying and selling. The market situation is stable.

Exchange Rates

British/American: This morning's foreign exchange market saw slight demand for the pound. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the American dollar was four dollars and ninety cents nine three seven five, which is point zero six two five higher than yesterday's closing price for the exchange rate between the American and British currencies. Afterwards it rose again six seven one five, the closing price was four dollars ninety-one cents five six two five.

British/French: The opening rose three pounds in sound, to seventy-four francs fifty-three, the closing was seventy-four francs fifty-six.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened quietly. Merchants were unwilling to operate, and the price fell five pounds in sound compared to the opening price due to the pressure of arbitrage. However, news of cotton crop damage still stabilized sentiment.

British Cotton: The cotton market situation today is firm. The closing price for January futures was six point eleven, which is five pounds in sound higher than yesterday's closing price.

British Wheat: Today's wheat price trended downwards. The closing price for December futures fell one and one-eighth pence to six shillings and five and a half pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market seems to regard the European situation as optimistic. In addition, telegraphs from Liverpool and Argentina were unsatisfactory, so the opening price plummeted. It initially fell one and a half cents, and then continued to fall one and a quarter cents due to multiple closures. The hearing price for bullish grain fell six two five, but the market situation still appeared stable when the telegram was sent.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was firm this morning. After the opening, the transaction price for January and March futures was six and a half pence, which is point zero six two five higher than yesterday's price. Although the midday market situation still had a firm and stable trend, it fell point zero six two five.

New York: Good news from London invigorated the New York rubber market. The opening price was three pounds in sound higher than yesterday's closing price, and then continued to rise six pounds in sound due to strong buying interest. After that, it became quiet.

Securities

New York: This morning's securities market, with the exception of a slight decline in mining stocks, the rest were strong, especially automobile stocks and railroad stocks. After the opening, railroad stocks and film stocks rose sharply. The average opening price of the Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average rose point six eight to one three five point eight one. Shantou Mayor Hosts Meeting with Various Circles to Explain Smuggling Case 74

Gan Jiehou and Wu Bosheng Arrive in Shantou, Li Yuanhe Says Negotiations Proceeding Smoothly

Shantou Correspondence: The case of Jieyang County government detaining smuggled foreign rice has caused a Sino-Japanese dispute. Currently, the Japanese attitude is still very tough. Six Japanese warships are still anchored in Shantou Port. Rear Admiral Shimomura, Commander of the 5th Squadron of the Japanese Fleet, is in charge of this case, and has been negotiating with the municipal government authorities on the command ship Ryūjō and at the Japanese Consulate in Shantou for several days. Gan Jiehou and Wu Bosheng, who were sent by the provincial authorities to Shantou to take charge of the negotiations, arrived in Shantou a few days ago, and immediately met with Shantou Mayor Li Yuanhe and Chao-Hai Customs Superintendent Zhang Jinghui, Commander Shimomura, and Japanese Consul Tanaka Ichiro stationed in Shantou to hold several sincere talks. The opinions of both parties have gradually converged. Wu Bosheng first returned to the province a few days ago with the terms of the negotiations agreed upon by both parties to request instructions. Therefore, the key to resolving this case still lies with the province. Li Yuanhe convened representatives from more than a dozen organizations such as Shantou reporters, lawyers, the North and South Port Guilds, and the Medical and Pharmaceutical Guilds at the Municipal Government Auditorium at approximately 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 11th. Li first reported, saying, "Recently, rumors have been spreading in the city, and citizens have been alarmed by each other. This is all unnecessary panic. After all, the only foreign incident that has occurred in Shantou recently is the Sino-Japanese dispute caused by the Jieyang County government detaining smuggled foreign rice. In this matter, the Japanese side's reason for negotiating with us is that we have violated international trade treaties. However, the smuggled foreign rice detained by the Jieyang County government was seized from stores in our country and has nothing to do with Japan. I have refuted this matter and am negotiating step by step, which is progressing smoothly. It is not as serious as the outside world has reported. This case can be resolved peacefully soon. All circles should feel at ease in their work and not be misled by rumors." At that time, two representatives from the Reporters Association inquired about the points of uncertainty about the case with Li. Li did not immediately answer due to time constraints and because the matter involved foreign negotiations and it was inconvenient to release information before it was resolved. The details of the negotiation are currently kept secret by the authorities and cannot be ascertained, and there are various reports circulating outside. However, the other party's demand for demarcation is indeed a fact, that is, they want to delineate the area below Xinxing Road as a special zone, and build wharves and warehouses at the end of Shenzhao Road, and also set a deadline of fourteen days for a reply. In recent days, Japanese sailors have often landed unarmed in groups and gathered at the Japanese Consulate and nearby Dongying Elementary School on Qilu Shenzhao Road. What they are doing is unknown. However, it is heard that Dongying Elementary School has already suspended classes. On the evening of the 11th, two teams of unarmed Japanese sailors, about thirty or forty people, went to the vicinity of the Chao-Shan Railway Station after landing, and hesitated slightly. The Shantou market is as quiet as usual, and it is expected that no accidents will occur. Fan Zhanpeng, Director of the Provincial Anti-Smuggling Office, arrived in Shantou from Hong Kong by boat on the 11th and went to the Anti-Smuggling Sub-Office to meet with the Sub-Office Director Xiao Sheng to inquire about the current situation of smugglers and anti-smuggling efforts. Then, he and Xiao took the Chao-Shan Railway to Chaoan to visit Division Commander Deng Longguang to discuss everything, and investigate the situation of smuggling in the Chaozhou and Shantou areas. It is heard that Fan plans to stay in Chaozhou and Shantou for a few days to thoroughly understand the inside story of the smugglers, and then return to the province to plan the entire method of preventing smuggling. (13th)

Boji Hospital Renamed Medical College to Commemorate Dr. Sun Yat-sen 75

Commemorative Conference on November 2nd, Also Holding the National Medical Association Annual Meeting

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangzhou Boji Hospital was established seventy-six years before the Republic of China (1835). Not only did it open a new era in Chinese medicine, but it was also the first hospital in the Far East to adopt Western medical techniques. In 1844, the first lithotomy was performed. In 1847, ether anesthesia was first used. The following year, chloroform was used. In 1875, the first abdominal surgery was performed. The earliest hospitals in the province, such as Haikou and Yangjiang, were all branch hospitals established by Boji. In the country, such as Xiamen, Shanghai, Beiping, Ningbo, and even neighboring Japan, eighty or ninety years ago, Boji doctors had successively transferred to practice medicine. The hospital was originally founded by British and American missionaries. Later, Dr. John Kerr came to serve as the director of the hospital. In 1855, a medical school was attached to the hospital. Initially, it only admitted male students. In 1879, at the request of the Zhenguang Girls' School, it also admitted female students, truly opening the beginning of co-education for men and women in China. At that time, the teaching method was only oral lectures and notes, and then medical books were translated. More than twenty kinds of translations were made successively, including "New Theory of the Body" and "Chemical Abstract", many of which are still worth exploring today. In particular, the treatment of gonorrhea by surgery is the most effective. An English annual report is published every year, briefly announcing the work of the year. Since 1920, it has been taken over by the Board of Directors of Lingnan University, and has become an organization of Chinese people. Dr. Sun Yat-sen began studying medicine at Boji Hospital. This year marks the 50th anniversary of his medical studies, and the centenary of the opening of Boji Hospital. Last year, Kong Xiangxi, Sun Ke, Zhong Rongguang, and others specially organized the Sun Yat-sen Medical College Preparatory Committee, and the National Government allocated funds to expand Boji Hospital and rename it Sun Yat-sen Medical College. A commemorative conference is scheduled to be held on November 2 of this year, on the one hand to commemorate the 100th anniversary of the arrival of Western medicine in China, and on the other hand to commemorate the 50th anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's medical studies and revolutionary movement. After the meeting on that day, the opening ceremony of the new college and the groundbreaking ceremony of the medical college will be held at the same time. During that week, it will also be the annual meeting of the Chinese Medical Association, and famous Chinese doctors will gather here at one time. It is truly an unprecedented initiative in the medical community.

Ban on Opium and Narcotics: Special Regulations for Punishment 76

Change of Jurisdiction for Opium Cases to Military Law; Directive from the General Headquarters to be Followed Uniformly Nationwide

Hankou Dispatch: Since assuming the position of Director-General of Opium Suppression, Chairman Chiang has paid increasing attention to the suppression of opium and narcotics. Considering that the penalties stipulated in the Opium Prohibition Law were relatively light and the judicial process was too lenient, which he believed would prevent the complete eradication of opium as scheduled, he specially formulated the Regulations for Punishing Opium and Narcotics Offenses. These regulations were submitted to the 479th Central Political Conference on the 16th and approved for record. Simultaneously, the Wuchang General Headquarters issued a directive to all provincial and municipal governments nationwide to comply with the regulations uniformly. The original directive stated in brief: "Strictly prohibiting opium and narcotics within a limited time and completely eliminating them is a consistent policy of our country throughout history. However, due to inconsistent authority, the results have not been significant. Furthermore, the spread of banditry and frequent local incidents have made it difficult to effectively eradicate opium and narcotics. Despite repeated orders from the government, the situation remains lax and the harm continues to deepen. This Commissioner is deeply alarmed and has therefore put forward the two-year opium prohibition policy, urging subordinates to implement it diligently. Therefore, in May of last year, the Nanchang General Headquarters first severely punished offenders involved in highly harmful opium substitutes, such as morphine, cocaine, heroin, red and white pills, and other similar narcotics. The Interim Regulations for the Strict Prohibition of Potent Narcotics were promulgated and circulated to all provinces, adopting the principle of using severe measures in times of disorder to deter others. After a year of implementation, it has shown significant effectiveness, gradually eliminating the harm of narcotics and transforming public morals. As for opium, repeated orders and laws have also been issued to strictly prohibit it. However, because the penalties stipulated in the Opium Prohibition Law are relatively light and the judicial process is too lenient, the people cling to their ingrained habits and lack the determination to cleanse themselves. The crime of smoking opium only results in fines or the lowest degree of imprisonment. The penalties for planting, transporting, selling, and trafficking are also light, which encourages unscrupulous people to exploit loopholes in the law and is incompatible with the method of controlling opium prohibition in stages. This Commissioner has been deeply concerned day and night, believing that it is necessary to change the course of action to facilitate progress and cope with the situation. Now, having received the government's solemn mandate to assume the important responsibility of opium suppression, I must earnestly implement the orders. Based on past experience in opium and narcotics suppression and the current environmental needs, and after consulting various old and new regulations, I have conducted detailed research, summarized, and supplemented them. I have drafted Interim Regulations for Punishing Opium and Narcotics Offenses and have changed the jurisdiction for opium cases to military law. All trials and reviews will be conducted according to military law procedures to increase efficiency and prevent disputes, thereby upholding the central government's intention to pay attention to opium suppression and entrust it to concurrent management. In addition to submitting the regulations to the National Government for promulgation and implementation, and requesting that the Opium Prohibition Law be abolished and the provisions of Chapter 20 of the new Criminal Law regarding opium offenses be suspended, I now order you to comply with the regulations. You must ensure that your subordinates strictly comply with these regulations from the date of their implementation and should widely inform the people in advance so that they are aware of the warnings and do not fall into the trap of criminal punishment. There is great hope in this."

Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway: Railway Ministry Recovers the Nanping Section for Self-Management 77

—Sending Ling Hongxun to Prepare for Engineering Matters—

Hangzhou Dispatch: The Nanyu section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway has failed to be completed on schedule due to obstacles such as banditry, floods, diseases, and epidemics. However, the track-laying work has progressed fairly quickly and is expected to be open to traffic in mid-November of this year. For the remaining Nanchang to Pingxiang section, the Railway Bureau originally planned to move the engineering office to Nanchang after the completion of the Yunan section project, transfer personnel from that section to work, and continue to extend westward, estimating that construction would begin next spring and be completed within two years. However, according to reliable information, the Ministry of Railways has decided to recover the section (Nanchang to Pingxiang) for self-management and to organize the Jiangxi-Hunan Railway Engineering Bureau to be responsible for constructing the section. The bureau headquarters will be located in Nanchang. It is reported that the Ministry of Railways has sent Ling Hongxun, director of the Zhushao section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Engineering Bureau, to begin preparations. As for the route of the section, the Ministry of Railways and the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway have repeatedly sent teams to measure and survey multiple routes. Detailed reports have been prepared regarding the mileage, engineering, and economic conditions along each route. The responsible authorities have conducted comparative studies based on the reports and are awaiting a final decision. It is reported that the originally considered routes included: (1) crossing the Yangtze River at Nanchang, passing through Wanzai and Liuyang to Changsha; (2) crossing the Yangtze River at Nanchang to Zhangshu, heading up the Yuan River to Pingxiang; (3) crossing the Yangtze River at Nanchang to Qingjiang, heading up the Yuan River to Pingxiang. After research, the first route was deemed to have the following drawbacks: (A) The Hengduan Mountains within Liuyang hinder construction; (B) There are large mountains across the Xiang River from Changsha, and the railway has no way out after crossing the Xiang River. Future extensions to Chongqing would have to detour across the Xiang River, and the curves and slopes of the old Zhuping Road from Pingxiang to Liling cannot be improved or connected. The second and third routes were also deemed unsuitable. In the future, one of the following two routes may be selected: (1) crossing the Yangtze River at Nanchang to Wanzai to Liling; (2) crossing the Yangtze River at Zhangshu through Yichun to Liling. Neither of these two routes passes through Pingxiang City.

According to Xie Longwen, deputy director and transportation section chief of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the operating income of the Hangyu section of the railway this year has not been as optimistic as expected due to various influences. For example, Quzhou and its surrounding counties were formerly famous paper-producing areas, and Jindong and its surrounding counties were known for their pig farming. Previously, exports were very strong, but now sales are sluggish and production has sharply decreased. Eastern Zhejiang is a fishing and salt-producing area, and in the past, domestic sales were also broad. Now, public salt collection has stopped, and private salt is rampant. All of these factors have affected freight transport. However, as the reputation of the Railway Bureau increases daily, it has gradually gained general trust. Therefore, the freight transport statistics for the past eight months of this year have still increased by 170,000 yuan compared to the same period last year. However, passenger transport has decreased by 80,000 yuan. According to general observation, passenger and freight transport may be expected to improve after the railway reaches Nanchang. However, eastern Jiangxi was severely affected by banditry in the past, and production has stopped. Although the remnants of the bandits have been suppressed, unburied corpses can still be found everywhere in the valleys and streams, emitting a foul odor. As a result, epidemics are rampant in various places, and many people, young and old, male and female, are suffering in their sickbeds. It will be difficult to revive the rural economy for a while. For these reasons, the business prospects after the opening of the Yunan section are not optimistic in the short term. The opening date of the section must be determined after the completion of the bridges is confirmed. The largest bridges in the section are those at Liangjiadu and Guixi. The Liangjiadu Bridge has one section with fourteen piers and another with five piers, both of which are nearing completion. The Guixi Bridge has twelve piers, but four piers have not been completed due to the rapid river current. The track-laying work has little left to be done, and the tracks can be connected in each section within days. Stone ballast engineering is currently underway. (18th)

What I Saw and Heard on My Journey West 78

—Song Hua

The Journey from Yichang to Chongqing

The section of the Yangtze River from Yichang to Chongqing is called the Sichuan River by the people of Sichuan. The Sichuan River is particularly difficult to navigate. In the past, river steamers traveled from the lower reaches of the Yangtze River to the upper reaches, with Yichang as the terminus and no further upstream. Water transportation above Yichang relied solely on wooden boats (i.e., sailboats). The river currents are very rapid, and it is very difficult for wooden boats to travel upstream. They could hardly move forward without boatmen pulling them along rugged mountain roads. When encountering cliffs on both sides, where boatmen could not pull the boats from the shore, they had to find a way to moor the boats and wait quietly for favorable winds before being able to raise sails and advance. Therefore, traveling from Yichang to Chongqing often took months. More than thirty years ago, a British person risked sailing a river steamer on the Sichuan River. After its success, the river steamer repeatedly encountered dangers and setbacks before gaining extensive experience in navigating the Sichuan River. Today, river steamers can travel freely on the Sichuan River without obstruction. When drinking water, one should remember the source, and it is truly impossible not to attribute the success to the arduous efforts of the predecessors. However, the gorges of the Sichuan River are strangely dangerous, and there are many dangerous shoals and hidden reefs. Therefore, river steamers on the Sichuan River can only travel during the day and moor at night, and no one dares to navigate at night. It takes four days to reach Chongqing from Yichang and only two days from Chongqing to Yichang because it is downstream.

River steamers traveling on the Sichuan River must have special river pilots on board to guide them. It is said that these river pilots come from the ranks of the "Tai Gong" on wooden boats. The so-called "Tai Gong" is the captain who commands the boatmen on wooden boats. They have special experience in the navigation routes of the Sichuan River and can understand where there are hidden reefs or shoals just by looking at the water patterns and waves in the river. River steamers need these river pilots for this reason. However, to become a river pilot, one must first pass the examination of the Customs and be given a license before assuming this position. Not every "Tai Gong" on a wooden boat can serve as a river pilot. As for why river steamers cannot navigate at night on the Sichuan River, it is because the river pilots cannot distinguish the water patterns and waves in the river at night. After a river steamer arrives in Yichang from the downstream, several river pilots board the ship. After boarding, they take turns guiding the helmsman, changing every three hours, fearing that prolonged viewing would cause blurred vision and endanger the river steamer. The special circumstances of river steamers traveling on the Sichuan River can be seen from this.

I boarded the "Minzheng" steamer on the 29th of last month and headed west from Yichang, first passing through the Xiling and Wushan Gorges. The mountains on both sides are very majestic and mostly cliffs. What is particularly strange is that when looking ahead from the bow of the ship, one only sees overlapping high mountains, rugged and towering, and *** fill the eyes. Therefore, traveling between mountain gorges can sometimes give people a feeling of "returning to the starting point." On this day, the scenery was all special mountain scenery and water colors. We also passed the magnificent Wushan Twelve Peaks, which broadened our horizons. The boat anchored in Wushan County at night.

The next day, we first passed the Qutang Gorge, Gate, Baidi City, and the Eight Trigrams Formation. Baidi City is where Liu Bei, the emperor of Shu Han, entrusted his son. The Eight Trigrams Formation is said to have been set up by Zhuge Liang. According to the ship's staff, there is a dry Eight Trigrams Formation on the shore and a water Eight Trigrams Formation in the river. What we saw on the boat was only the latter. In the afternoon, we passed Yunyang, and across from it was the "Lord Zhang Temple," which worships Zhang Fei. The temple is very magnificent, and on the wall facing the river are the four large characters "Jiang Shang Qing Feng" (Clear Breeze on the River), written by the famous calligrapher Peng Yunbo. The brushstrokes are strong and vigorous. When viewed from the boat, the calligraphy is very clear. It is said that there is also Zhang Fei's head in the temple, stored in an oil jar. If oil is poured in, the head will float out. Whether this is believable is still uncertain. The boat rested in Wanxian at night.

On the 1st of this month, we passed Zhongzhou and Yinshan (also known as Shibaozhai). There are pagodas and temples on the mountain, said to be the hometown of Qin Liangyu, a famous female general of the late Ming Dynasty. On this day, I talked with Commissioner Liu of the Postal Service, who was on the same boat, about the situation in Sichuan. He said that he had gone to the counties of Youyang, Pengshui, Xiushan, and Qianjiang in southern Sichuan last year on official business. There were many bandits in the area, and he narrowly escaped disaster. Later, he asked the Public Security Bureau to send armed police to escort him before he dared to complete his official duties in various places. There is a Sichuan saying, "There is no need to teach a son, just let him travel to You, Xiu, Qian, and Peng once." This is because traveling to these four counties can provide many special experiences. These four counties and their vicinity have mineral resources and many wasteland areas. If they are developed to benefit the people, it would be a way to eliminate banditry. We passed Fengdu City at sunset. There are temples such as the Heavenly Son Hall and the Qin King Hall in the city. There are also two white pagodas along the river, facing each other diagonally, which can be seen from the boat. It is said that the two pagodas have yin and yang divisions, which is a superstitious belief. Commissioner Liu said that foolish men and women often go to the temples to buy talismans and "road guides" (passports for the underworld). The temple thus earns a special income. According to the book "Yichang to Chongqing" compiled by the Bank of China, there are two reasons why people mistakenly believe that Fengdu has the underworld: (1) Wang Fangping of the Former Han Dynasty and Yin Changsheng of the Later Han Dynasty once practiced Taoism on Pingdu Mountain in the county, so some people called it Yinwang Mountain. Later, it was falsely spread that this mountain had the King of the Underworld. (2) The county has the Xiantu Temple and the Wuyao Cave, which Taoists call the "Zifu Zhenxian." Therefore, some people mistakenly believe that Fengdu is not a place for ordinary people. Therefore, some people associate Fengdu with a fairyland or the underworld. In fact, Fengdu is clearly a human world, with no underworld or fairyland. Our country has too many illiterate people, and superstition has not been broken, which is regrettable. After the boat passed Fengdu, it sailed to the small town of Tongyuan Temple for the night.

On the 2nd, the boat passed through the Scissors Gorge, Fuling, and Changshou. Although there are still high mountains on both sides, they are not as magnificent as those seen on the first and second days after leaving Yichang. It rained on this day, and we saw large and small waterfalls on the mountains on both sides, like dancing white ribbons. The moment on the mountainside was like smoke, like mist, and like catkins, which was a wonderful sight. There were many sailboats in the river. Some of the boats had flags inserted, which were said to be镖 flags, indicating that the boat was insured by so-and-so and that the passengers and cargo were safer. Many boatmen on these sailboats traveling up the Yangtze River often pulled the boats naked on the shore. When encountering cliffs, they immediately jumped into the water to board the boat, which was very difficult and pitiful. Mr. Chen, an employee of the Bank of China on the same boat, had traveled to various places in Sichuan and told me that he had seen large sailboats on the Jialing River, each with dozens of boatmen pulling them. When the boatmen pulled the boats, they were completely naked in warm weather, not wearing a single thread. In cool weather, they only wore short clothes and no trousers. However, their steps were neat, and they sang mountain songs in unison, like boatmen's songs, just like a very disciplined army. Their singing was quite loud, and the tone was tragic. He also said that the poor people in Sichuan were very bitter, and the lives of miners and boatmen were particularly bitter. Green forest heroes who committed crimes and repented often joined the work of miners and boatmen, because it was not easy to be arrested either by mining underground or by traveling to various places with ships. Mr. Mo Dehui was also on the same boat to Chongqing. In the afternoon, I chatted with Mr. Mo. We first talked about the North China issue and diplomatic issues, and then we talked about the national economic issue. Mr. Mo expressed deep sorrow at seeing foreign ships freely entering and leaving the Yangtze River, saying that if China could not increase tariffs, it would be difficult to stop the leak of wealth, and the poverty of the people and the exhaustion of wealth were by no means accidental. During the chat, the boat traveled very slowly, even slower than a sailboat. Someone came to report, "The ship's engine is damaged, and it may be difficult to reach Chongqing today." Mr. Mo sighed and said, "We are all in a leaky boat." The meaning of his words was ambiguous, and everyone who heard it was moved. Fortunately, the ship's engine was soon repaired and was able to continue sailing as usual. It reached its destination at six o'clock in the afternoon (Chongqing is a full hour behind Shanghai; at that time, Shanghai was only five o'clock). It was already dusk. By the time we hired a small boat, crossed the river, and landed, thousands of lights were already lit.

Wuxi: Tobacco and Alcohol Licenses Do Not Need to Affix Stamps 81

Xu Ruzhou, standing committee member of the local Wine and Sauce Shop Association, and Shi Qinglin, standing committee member of the Tobacco Exchange Association, previously submitted a request because Article 3 of the new Stamp Tax Law stipulates that certificates issued by government agencies for collecting taxes may be exempt from affixing stamps. They requested the Ministry of Finance to issue an order to exempt them from affixing stamps. Yesterday, they received a response from the Ministry of Finance, stating that tobacco and alcohol licenses are exempt from affixing stamps in accordance with Article 3, Item 2 of the new Stamp Tax Law, and approved the issuance of an order to the subordinates for uniform compliance.

Hangzhou: Spring Cocoon Silk Reeling Very Profitable 86

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction Cocoon and Silk Control Committee collected approximately 100,000 dan of fresh cocoons in the spring of this year and entrusted them to silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces with relatively complete equipment for reeling. It is expected to be completely completed by mid-November. A total of 3,800 dan of silk were reeled. All bank loans of 580,000 yuan have been repaid. As for the sale of raw silk in Shanghai, 740 dan were sold in June at a price of 444.40 yuan per dan, 1,151 dan were sold in July at a price of 460.88 yuan per dan, and 875 dan were sold in August at a price of 521.76 yuan per dan. A total of 2,770 dan of raw silk were sold, with an average price of 476.4 yuan per dan, totaling 1,318,900 yuan. After calculating the income and expenditure of spring cocoon silk reeling and sales, there is a surplus of more than 100,000 yuan.

Recently, due to the impact of the economic downturn, transactions have declined, and most brokers have gone out of business. It is difficult to continue to maintain the exchange. A shareholders' meeting was convened on the 17th, and it was decided to dissolve the exchange. Sun Xingzhi, Zhou Dali, and five others were appointed as liquidators.

President Sun Arrives in Shanghai and Discusses the Legislative Yuan's Amendment to the Draft Constitution 88

Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, accompanied by Xu Shiying, Chairman of the National Government Relief Committee, Liu Weichi, Vice Minister of Industry, Zou Lin, Vice Minister of Finance, and Legislative Yuan members Ma Yinchu and others, left Nanjing by night train at 11:00 PM on the 8th and arrived in Shanghai. He arrived at Zhenru Station at 7:10 AM on the 19th and immediately returned to his private residence on Columbia Road for rest. According to Sun, the National Congress should be convened once every two years according to the party constitution. The Fifth National Congress should have been convened in 1933, but it was postponed for one year due to the national crisis. It was later postponed again for another year for various reasons. Therefore, it has now been decided to convene it as scheduled. The Central Committee has decided on the principle of amending the draft constitution and has handed it over to the Legislative Yuan for amendment. The Legislative Yuan is scheduled to meet next week to discuss it. Once the amendment is completed, it will be submitted to the Central Standing Committee for approval and then submitted to the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee for discussion.

Rescuing Ships in Distress 94

Yesterday, one ocean-going ship and one river steamer were in distress and reported to their respective head offices in Shanghai. Rescue efforts are currently underway. Details are as follows:

Beihua: The Beilun ship of the Northern Shipping Company, with a deadweight of 1,378.89 tons and a length of 206 English feet, has compartments that can hold 17,000 bags of grain. It usually operates on the Northern Seas route. This time, it was going to Zhenjiang to transport grain to Tianjin and was originally scheduled to go directly to North China without coming to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, shortly after the ship left Zhenjiang, its engine rudder suddenly broke down, and the Beihua lost its ability to move. The shipowner felt that it was very dangerous due to the heavy load and the broken engine rudder. Yesterday, he sent an urgent telegram to Shanghai for help. Upon receiving the news, the Shanghai company immediately sent a tugboat to Zhenjiang to tow the Beihua back to Shanghai.

Huaxing: The Huaxing ship of the Huaxin Shipping Company is currently loading salt in Haizhou. Yesterday, news was received in Shanghai that the ship was stranded in Haizhou due to the tide receding. The shipowners and others repeatedly tried to find ways to drive it out of the shallows but were unsuccessful. They are now waiting for the tide to rise to try to leave the shallows.

Dalu: The Dalu ship of the Dalu Industrial Company, fully loaded with coal, was coming to Shanghai from Jiujiang and was stranded in Tongzhou. Upon receiving the news in Shanghai, a tugboat has been sent to tow and rescue it.
