Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

From "Save the Middle School Students" to National Salvation Education 225

— Liu Xin

Because Ms. Chen Hengzhe investigated the opinions of elementary school children's parents on current school education in the "Independent Review," and at the same time discovered that middle school students have no way to cope with their heavy workload day and night, Ms. Chen lamented the loss of life of the nation's future masters and issued a call to "Save the Middle School Students." The words came from the heart, making it even more shocking. What I admire is the slogan put forward by Ms. Chen: "Save the Middle School Students," but I want to save middle school students for other reasons, because I think what Ms. Chen sees is only one side of the current middle school education, not the whole picture.

We admit that education is life, education is growth, education cannot educate students to go astray, and even more cannot educate students to become dead people, so trying to help seedlings grow by pulling them up is the view of fools. In the principles of education, the psychological development and the physiological development should be consistent, which has almost become an iron rule. If one is ignorant of this point, or promotes premature development of students, or hinders their physiological health, it can be said to be extremely sinful. But if we investigate the actual situation of middle school education in our country now, whether in terms of curriculum, teaching materials, teaching methods, or life, has it all reached above a reasonable level? This becomes a very big question.

The new curriculum standards were formulated by educational experts hired by the Ministry of Education and ordered to be implemented. Although the government is determined to strive for rationality, the standards set may not fully meet the actual needs and there is no waste, and the quantity may not exactly match the students' ability to bear, and there is no excess or deficiency. As for teaching materials, although there are curriculum standards to follow, most of the textbooks are printed by private workshops. The subjectivity of one person or a few people cannot be avoided. The quantity, content, and time coordination often become their own theories. If we talk about teaching methods, because they directly affect students' interest in learning, the difference in teaching efficiency may not necessarily stop at one out of a hundred. Furthermore, the relationship between students' daily life and learning cannot be ignored: with a good learning environment, it is easier to achieve learning results; with a disciplined and happy life, learning can proceed in a regular manner. In these aspects, middle school students are indeed being used as passive test subjects: they cannot know for themselves how to discard impractical courses, they cannot choose for themselves how to cut down uneconomical teaching materials, and they do not even know how to replace teachers who do not have good teaching methods. What is most heartbreaking is that in Shanghai, the center of culture, middle schools are densely packed, but it can be asserted that there are almost no schools with complete facilities that provide a good learning environment for students. Students are all infected with a frivolous and impractical atmosphere, arrogant and romantic. Since it is impossible to sit still, let alone cope with heavy work! Although this is only one corner of current education, it is precisely because there is this corner that Ms. Chen Hengzhe's appeal should not only be to "Save the Middle School Students" by relieving the heavy workload, but also to issue a cry for help for the middle school students who are sinking into unreasonable suffering!

Today's middle school students are the lifeline of the future nation and the backbone of future national construction. Naturally, we need the lifeline of the future nation or the backbone of future national construction to be strong and robust, and the body can withstand hardships. However, at the same time, we also need the lifeline of the future nation or the backbone of national construction to be intelligent and capable, and their wisdom is sufficient to cope with the great difficulties of the future. Therefore, I still think that the education that most middle school students receive is not enough in degree and not strict enough!

No country's secondary education has ever been as scattered and low as ours, and no country's middle school students' lives have ever been as unrestrained as ours. We do not necessarily have to imitate the strict military national education of others, but at least in this era when the country is in danger of destruction at any moment, everyone needs to be able to shoulder the burden of national salvation and survival, and a serious national salvation education needs to be implemented!

Save the Middle School Students! Like Ms. Chen Hengzhe, I am also appealing for the hundreds of thousands of middle school students sinking in the sea of suffering across the country.

Common Knowledge

The North and South Poles 226

— Yi Kun

If you go to an old villager and say, "There are two places in the world where half the year is day and half the year is night," then you will definitely be greatly ridiculed. However, in reality, there are indeed such two places in the world, namely the North and South Poles; because of the relationship between the Earth and the Sun, the South Pole is night for the first half of the year and day for the second half of the year, while the North Pole is day for the first half of the year and night for the second half of the year. At the same time, most of the South Pole is a landmass; called the world's smallest "sixth continent," surrounded by oceans, while most of the North Pole is occupied by the smallest ocean—the Arctic Ocean—surrounded by land: this is the main difference between the North and South Poles. However, these two polar regions also have many points in common. What is generally known is that the climate of both the North and South Poles is very cold. In winter, the temperature in these two polar regions is often tens of degrees below freezing. All liquids, even alcohol, have frozen into hard blocks. Temperatures above freezing can only be enjoyed for a very short time of the year here. However, believe it or not, the coldest place in the world is not the North and South Poles, but southeastern Siberia, where the climate is more than ninety degrees below zero Fahrenheit, which is truly terrifying!

In the eyes of people who are already well-fed and clothed, although the North and South Poles are very cold, the scenery is very beautiful. Here are snow-white icebergs, crystal-clear ice pillars, and gray-white wildernesses, reflecting in our eyes a silver world. In the coastal areas of Antarctica, when the sun is covered by thin clouds in the south and the world is as quiet as a dream, you can see icebergs and ice dikes emerging from the gray-black sea surface to the north: some are with cold purple-white colors, and some are illuminated by the sun, like golden walls. When the strong wind is blowing, the air and the water surface make a loud noise, as if a group of leopards are constantly roaring, making people feel extremely nervous and feeling the greatness of nature? Draw the North Pole, of course, you can also see the sun, but the sun seen here is at the horizon. The situation in the South Pole is the opposite. Therefore, the scenery presented by these two polar regions is also somewhat different. However, the poetic natural beauty of the two poles is the same. If you have time to visit the North and South Poles, then you will feel that the natural beauty of snow, snow, and sea waves... that many poets have sung is not worth mentioning.

Most of the people living in the polar regions are Eskimos and a small number of Samoans. They live in igloos and make a living by fishing and hunting. They are still a barbaric people. Although some Europeans and Americans have come here in modern times to explore and fish, they are by no means the main residents of the polar regions. As for how human life in these two polar regions will be in the future, it will be judged by the continued efforts of mankind to fight against nature.

Antarctic exploration is a great feat of mankind in the past fifty years, but the history of Arctic exploration is quite old. As early as 345 BC, the sailor Pytheas of Massalia sailed to the "North Sea," telling the story of the long nights and the state of the swimming world here. Later in history, there were some explorations of the Arctic, but the true discovery of the value of the Arctic was after Columbus discovered the New World. Because of the development of capitalism, the shipping industry needed to find a northern sea route from Europe to eastern Asia, so the Arctic region was discovered. Initially, the Arctic passage was discovered in the 16th century, and then whaling ships gradually came and went, so the various places within the Arctic Circle were gradually known to people. In the 19th century, Ross discovered the North Magnetic Pole in northern North America, Franklin discovered the Northwest Passage from northern North America to eastern Asia, and Lansian crossed the Arctic Ocean and reached a point at 86 degrees 13 minutes and 36 seconds north latitude. The Italian Kakkuni also reached 86 degrees 24 minutes north latitude. All these discoveries not only made mankind more aware of the Arctic region, but also greatly helped the development of science. By the 20th century, the Arctic region aroused even more interest from mankind, and explorers became more advanced, so many places in the Arctic became more known. Recently, the Soviet Union has used great efforts to continuously explore the Arctic, so as to conquer nature with its great new power. As for Antarctic exploration, it was prevalent in the 19th century, and the British, Americans, and Swedes have made important discoveries. In 1929, the United States organized an expedition led by Byrd, landed from the Ross Sea to Whale Bay to reach Antarctica, and established the Little America colony here; and on the Ross Ice Shelf, created new Antarctic houses, radio stations and airfields. In the future, with the continuous efforts of mankind, the value of the North and South Poles will surely be greater.

The North and South Poles are not only significant in terms of human transportation, but also have abundant products. In Antarctica, the output of moss, seals, seabirds, diamonds, and coal is very abundant, and the place called Whale Bay is truly worthy of its name. There are many whales in the offshore area, and the output of seagulls and seabirds is also extremely abundant. Therefore, many Europeans and even Japanese people go to catch whales by whaling ships, and many of them have made a fortune. As for the Arctic region, it produces trees, moss, wild animals, wild birds, seals, whales, and coal, which are also attracting attention. However, these are only the current discoveries. As for what is hidden under the two thousand feet of ice, and what animals are buried under the land, there is no way to know now. Therefore, these two "strange places," places where half the year is day and half the year is night, and places that are frozen for a long time, are attracting much attention from countries around the world; here, as elsewhere, the struggle between the powers is very fierce.

At a time when the powers are working hard to prepare for a war to re-divide the world's colonies, some people hope that everyone will work hard to develop the North and South Poles and move the surplus population of various countries to the polar regions: although this method cannot avoid war, the effort of mankind to reduce the mutual struggle between mankind and concentrate the power of all mankind to conquer nature is a great leap in the evolution of mankind. Now, there are still many treasures in the world, not just a part of the North and South Poles? If the power of all mankind is concentrated to develop it, it can make everyone's life happy. The reason why it is not so old now is because mankind is still fighting each other, making it impossible for everyone to concentrate their efforts to deal with nature. Therefore, when we talk about the North and South Poles, we hope that everyone will work hard to turn the struggle between people into the struggle of all mankind against nature.

Various Industry Surveys

The Sichuan Province Wholesale Piece Goods and Sundries Trade 227

— You Song

The "imported goods" of "piece goods and sundries" sold in various cities of Sichuan Province can be said to be entirely wholesaled from Shanghai. Larger commercial firms with more capital generally send a shrewd, capable, and steady partner to represent them in Shanghai to purchase goods. Smaller shops, due to economic constraints, either entrust others to act as their agent or purchase goods wholesale from larger firms. The representatives stationed in Shanghai are known in the commercial field as "Zhuang Ke" (resident buyers). They mostly reside in inns located in convenient transportation areas near commercial districts, to facilitate "receiving goods" and "shipping goods" (such as the "Yi Ji Inn" near Dai Gou Bridge and the "Hui Ji" on Wu Ma Road, are the resident locations of the Sichuanese piece goods and sundries traders). Their method of purchasing goods, except for a few cases that require direct negotiation with manufacturers or companies, is mainly through the solicitations of "Ju Ke" ("wholesale salesmen" from various manufacturers or companies). After the goods are transported to the inn and checked, the "Zhuang Ke" find people to pack them into parcels (commonly called "Da Bao"), which are then handed over to the post office or merchant ships for transportation back to Sichuan to be sold by their firms. The purchase and transportation involve many procedures and incur a lot of costs. Therefore, "piece goods and sundries from Shanghai" (and other goods as well) are at least one-third more expensive when they reach Sichuan, and sometimes almost twice as expensive.

However, even with rising prices, many "piece goods and sundries firms" still do not make much profit, and many even lose money and are forced to close down! What is the reason for this? It is said that half of the reason is due to the constant warfare among Sichuan warlords, with cities devastated by cannon and machine gun fire, and heavy taxes further bankrupting the rural areas. Most people have lost their purchasing power, which has obstructed the sale of goods! At the same time, because exchange rates and transportation costs are too high, the cost of purchasing goods for various firms is too high, so even raising market prices is of no use.

1. High Exchange Rates: Sichuanese merchants purchase goods in Shanghai using funds remitted through the post office or banks. Because of the complex political situation in Sichuan and the financial disorder, remittances to Shanghai always incur a heavy exchange rate loss. In the past few years, it cost about 300 yuan per 1,000 yuan. Last year, during the tense military situation, it rose to 600 or 700 yuan per 1,000 yuan. Under such shockingly high exchange rates, many firms even lost their capital, and the "Zhuang Ke" quickly stopped buying goods, bringing the entire business to a standstill. How can one expect to make a profit? Although the situation in Sichuan is now relatively stable and finances are being reorganized, the exchange rate still requires 60 to 70 yuan.

2. Expensive Freight Charges: According to the post office regulations, parcels sent to Sichuan Province are exceptionally expensive. Moreover, because the conditions in various regions of Sichuan are different, freight charges are divided into two levels of treatment. The minimum is also to charge ("

Page 25

Double the Rate"), where each parcel weighing 44 pounds requires a postage fee of four yuan and some cents; the maximum is "Triple the Rate," where a parcel of the same weight requires six yuan and some cents. Among them, the post office considers transportation to be relatively convenient in counties such as Tingjin, Hechuan, Hejiang, Luzhou, Nanxi, and Yibin, and therefore charges "Double the Rate" for each parcel, while counties such as Fushun, Neijiang, Longchang, and Guang'an are charged "Triple the Rate." Originally, merchants already felt that the "Double the Rate" was too high. Merchants in counties charged "Triple the Rate" felt even more burdened! Because the weight of "piece goods and sundries" is relatively high, it doesn't take much to pack a parcel to the required weight. Moreover, the quantity and frequency of shipments are high, so the transportation costs are considerable, which increases costs!

In fact, in addition to the post office, goods can also be transported by boat, which is cheaper. If shipped through the post office, "one piece of goods" (twelve parcels make one piece) calculated at the "Triple Rate," would cost 78 yuan. If shipped by boat, including water freight and transshipment fees, it only costs 9 or 10 yuan (before the export tax was exempted). Therefore, merchants in areas such as Fushun, Longchang, Neijiang, and Guang'an, which are charged the triple rate, ship silk and wool fabrics and sundries by post separately to reduce costs, while cotton fabrics are shipped by boat. Since the implementation of the unified tax system on August 1 of this year, the export tax of 17 yuan and 50 cents per piece of cotton fabric has been exempted. Therefore, each piece of goods can be reduced by more than 27 yuan compared to shipping by post. As a result, the "Zhuang Ke" in these counties are now also shipping silk and wool fabrics by boat! However, the procedures for shipping by boat are troublesome and time-consuming, and after the boat arrives in Chongqing, it still needs to be transshipped (by land). Therefore, they still hope that the post office can reduce the rates and treat them the same as Hejiang and Luzhou counties so that they can ship by post.

Not long ago, the "Zhuang Ke" of the "Shanghai-based Piece Goods and Sundries Traders from Sichuan" once jointly submitted a written request to the Shanghai Postal Administration Bureau to ask the head office to reduce the "Triple Rate" for Fushun, Neijiang, Longchang, Guang'an, and other counties to the "Double Rate." The reasons given were: Fushun, Neijiang, and Guang'an are located on the waterfront, and water transportation is considered convenient. Longchang and Zigong, although inland, have roads accessible to automobiles, and transportation is not too difficult. In theory, they should be treated the same as Hejiang and Hechuan counties. They also said that if parcels from these counties cannot be transported directly to their destination and must be transshipped midway, resulting in higher costs, Hejiang and Luzhou counties also require transshipment, so why are the fees lower? If it is because these counties are farther away, then some counties in northwestern Sichuan are over 1,000 li away, so why are they also charged only the "Triple Rate"? The reasons for their request for a reduction in fees seemed sufficient. Therefore, on the 14th of the previous month, the Shanghai Postal Administration Bureau replied: "This bureau's collection of parcel rates is based on the cost of transportation. The cost of transporting parcels to Longchang and other places is indeed higher than to Hechuan and other places, so a unified rate is charged... Furthermore, after investigating, the number of parcels sent to Longchang and other places last month was very small. If the parcel rates for these places were reduced to a single rate, would there be a sufficient increase in the number of parcels sent to these places? Please investigate and reply regarding the approximate increase in numbers, which should exceed what percentage of ten? Please investigate and reply so that it can be forwarded to the Nanjing headquarters for review..." After receiving this reply, the merchant immediately replied to the questions raised by the post office, saying that if the goods from counties such as Fushun and Neijiang were all sent by post, there would be more than 10,000 parcels per year. Although the number of parcels sent by post in August was reduced, it was because postage was too expensive and shipping offered reduced export taxes, making it much cheaper to ship by boat. If the post office could reduce a single rate, then silk and wool fabrics and sundries currently shipped by boat could all be sent by post, which would lead to significant progress in the parcel business. Recently, the post office has again provided a formal written reply, stating that the parcel rate for Neijiang, Longchang, and other counties has been reduced to "one and a half single rates" on October 7. Other places such as Fushun, Guang'an, and Zigong still need to submit separate documents to be handled further. However, the Sichuan traders feel that they have not achieved their goal, and even some counties have not been reduced at all, so they will continue to request a reduction. They believe that the post office's regulations were originally based on the transportation conditions in various regions, so the parcel rates for Sichuan vary. However, these regulations are only applicable to the Sichuan of the past, where "the road to Shu is difficult, more difficult than ascending to heaven." Now the road to Shu is no longer "difficult," and various counties have new-style roads with long-distance buses running regularly, so transportation is undoubtedly very convenient. The transportation of parcels is not difficult, so these regulations should be changed according to the current transportation conditions in Sichuan.

Scientific Miscellany

The Physical Effects of Table Salt in Living Bodies 228

— Quyang

Salt is essential for everyone. Like rice, noodles, vegetables, and meat, it has become one of humanity's primary foods. But what exactly does salt do for our bodies? Most ordinary people do not know, so I would like to briefly discuss this as a piece of common scientific knowledge.

So-called table salt, its chemical formula is a sodium atom and a chlorine atom combined, in chemistry it is called sodium chloride. If we separate these two elements by electrical polarity, then sodium is positively charged, and chlorine is negatively charged. When they are each broken down and exist independently, they become ions, sodium becomes a positive ion, and chlorine becomes a negative ion. When table salt is dissolved in water, the dispersed crystals may still maintain the salt molecule state, but most of the molecules have sodium atoms and chlorine atoms separated into ions. Everyone knows that positive and negative electricity attract each other. Current is conducted through the proximity of these two differently charged ions, so these ions become good conductors. They themselves are also moving extraordinarily actively. All chemical reactions are not molecular affairs, but are caused by the interaction between ions. This, in analyzing the number and arrangement of electrons in the organizational state of atoms, is consistent with the theory that chemical reactions occur through the action of the outer electrons. Since ions are the tools that facilitate chemical reactions, the chemical reactions within living bodies must rely on ions to act in between to make them actively occur, which goes without saying. If there are no chemical reactions in the living body, then all metabolism, heat energy and vitality, and so on will cease.

Since ions are so important to living bodies, let us now examine the role of the ions decomposed from table salt in living bodies, and we can know one part of the importance of salt to life. The ions produced by the dissociation of mercury compounds, such as Hg, have a great bactericidal effect, which is naturally very important. But what about the sodium ions produced by the dissociation of table salt? It is also very important. Although it does not have a drastic effect on protoplasm, there are many sodium ions present in the tissue fluid. This kind of sodium ion has an extremely strong active inductive property, so it has an excitatory effect on the nerves. Sodium has almost become the basic condition for supporting the excitability of living bodies. If our bodies lack the components of table salt, then people will become languid and depressed to the point of lifelessness. So the saying that not eating salt causes lack of energy has a corresponding reason. Like sodium and potassium ions, because it has the ability to move actively, it can improve all metabolic processes. Not only are sodium ions in table salt very important to living bodies, but among the various negative ions in living bodies, chlorine ions are the most numerous in the blood and tissues, and they are also indispensable for general life functions. Since living bodies have the positive electrical charge possessed by positive ions, there must be negative electrical charge ions to neutralize them in order to maintain electrical balance, which is also extremely important for life phenomena.

Why does salt have such an important effect on living bodies? This is governed by a physical relationship. Living bodies are not completely liquid or solid, but a kind of colloidal substance that can become solid. Because the important life core of a living body is the cell. If this thing, the cell, comes into contact with water, it becomes round. According to the law of minimum surface area, surface tension occurs, which is governed by the laws of liquids. But cells are also capable of self-differentiation, and cell division is this effect, so it is also governed by the laws of solids and has the properties of solids. Because of this, most living bodies are colloidal.

Since living bodies are living entities in a colloidal state, they must maintain appropriate moisture and must exchange substances with external objects, and regulate their excretion and absorption in order to maintain their life. Therefore, the permeability of cell tissues is very important. However, this permeability is still a special physical effect of colloidal bodies, and it also changes due to the influence of external substances, so it is necessary to make it a suitable change for the needs of life. However, the substance solution that can maintain this appropriate regulatory effect is most suitable for a moderately saline solution. Because the osmotic pressure generated by salts is very strong, the power to absorb moisture is also very strong. If the cell has an appropriate amount of salt to maintain a certain amount of moisture, the tension of the cell is moderate. If the moisture is too little, its tension will also decrease, which means that the cell will lose its active life ability.

In the normal state, the osmotic pressure inside the cell is equal to the osmotic pressure inside the tissue fluid. This is because the salt concentration inside the cell is equal to the salt concentration outside the cell. If this equilibrium is broken, the living body will experience obstacles to life and create danger. Because of this, salt has become an indispensable food every day, but it should not be eaten too much. There is experimental evidence to prove that if a piece of raw meat is immersed in a very concentrated salt solution, the muscles will shrink, and its volume will be greatly reduced. Conversely, if this piece of meat is immersed in salt water with a lower salt solution concentration than that inside the meat cells, the meat will swell and its volume will increase. Also, if frog meat is immersed in sucrose water with the same osmotic pressure as frog blood, its excitability will decrease, even to the point of complete unresponsiveness. If this meat is then taken out and placed in physiological saline, its excitability will recover very quickly. There is no other reason for this, because the former lacks sodium ions in the sucrose solution, and the physiological saline has appropriate sodium ions, so one cannot cause another reaction due to electrical ion activity, and one can cause a reaction due to electrical ion activity. One presents a living barrier phenomenon, and the other can make the living body comfortably maintain its vitality. In the former example, it is because the cells are in a concentrated salt solution, because the liquid concentration is too high, and the ion activity is very strong. Instead, it frequently offends the membrane skin to give a high osmotic pressure, but it cannot pass through this membrane. However, this semi-permeable cell membrane can allow water with strong permeability to pass through alone. Therefore, if the salt concentration in the tissue fluid is greater than the concentration inside the cells, the water molecules inside the cells are drawn out by the salt, causing the cells to shrink. Conversely, if the tissue fluid has a lower concentration than the salt solution inside the cells, then the moisture in the tissue fluid will fully penetrate into the cells, and the cells will grow. Only physiological saline can give cells a suitable culture and maintain their excitability and appropriate physiological state. Otherwise, such as while blood cells in a concentrated saline solution will shrink due to loss of water, while in an over-diluted saline solution will swell and rupture due to the penetration of too much water. When a person eats too much salt and feels thirsty, the reason is simply that the moisture in the whole body's cells is excessively absorbed by the concentrated salt solution in the body fluid, resulting in a feeling of water shortage. Also, when we coat raw meat with a large amount of salt, it can prevent it from rotting. This is also because the moisture in the cells has been absorbed, making it dry and unsuitable for microorganisms to survive. The ability of cured meat to tighten the meat is the same principle.

But how much salt should humans eat as most appropriate? That is to say, what percentage of salt is appropriate for physiological saline that is suitable for protecting the body? According to scientific observation, a salt water with a salt content of one percent is most suitable for a saline solution that can match the osmotic pressure of cells. All higher temperature objects are suitable for one percent or 0.96, while frogs and cold-blooded animals are suitable for 0.6 to 0.7, otherwise there is a danger of shrinking blood cells, and if it is insufficient, there is a danger of rupturing blood cells, both of which are harmful to life.

Economic Transactions

Recent Economic Situation in the Nordic Countries 229

— Jie Zhi

Generally speaking, since last year, the economies of the Nordic countries such as Norway, Finland, Sweden, and Denmark have shown signs of improvement. This phenomenon has continued until this year.

First of all, looking at the trade situation of the Nordic countries, with the exception of Norway's exports decreasing somewhat, the trade volume of other countries in the first half of this year has increased compared to the same period last year. However, last year's trade increase was only due to an increase in exports, while this year's increase in imports is even greater than its exports: this can be said to be a significant difference in the trade situation in these two years. From the following table, we can know that this year, Denmark, Sweden, and Norway's import surpluses have all increased dramatically, while Finland's trade has also turned from an export surplus to an import surplus.

First half of 1934:

Imports Exports Balance Difference

Sweden (10,000 Kronor) 610 569 41 (Import Surplus)

Denmark (10,000 Kronor) 629 576 53 (Import Surplus)

Norway (10,000 Kronor) 371 283 88 (Import Surplus)

Finland (10,000 Finnish Marks) 2,187 2,268 181 (Export Surplus)

First half of 1935:

Imports Exports Import Surplus

Sweden (10,000 Kronor) 658 571 87

Denmark (10,000 Kronor) 646 604 42

Norway (10,000 Kronor) 382 277 105

Finland (10,000 Finnish Marks) 2,402 2,375 25

With the exception of Denmark, the increase in this import surplus can be said to be a normal phenomenon. For example, Finland's trade, the import surplus in the first half of this year is normal, while its huge export surplus in the first half of last year was an exception. Sweden's import surplus can largely be offset by its foreign investment income, and Norway's import surplus can also be offset by its shipping income. In the case of Denmark, its international balance of payments was already small last year, with expenditure exceeding income; this year, because agricultural products, which are major exports, are quite sluggish, there is even less hope for improving its international balance of payments.

At the same time, it is most noteworthy that the increase in imports is the significant increase in raw materials. This trend could be seen last year, and it has become more obvious this year. From this, we can imagine that the domestic industry in the Nordic countries has indeed improved in recent years.

In fact, Sweden's import prices for food and textiles have decreased by about 14 million Kronor compared to before, while its import of machinery has soared from 26 million Kronor to 50 million Kronor. At the same time, imports of automobiles and ships have increased by about 18 million Kronor, and imports of metals and metal products have also increased by 16 million Kronor. Finland's imports of machinery and equipment have increased by about 110 million Marks, imports of metals and metal products have increased by 87 million Marks, and imports of transportation equipment have also increased by 29 million Marks; while its imports of food and textiles have also decreased. The situation in Norway is the same, with imports of ships and machinery also soaring. — From this, it is clear that Norway, Sweden, and Finland have been making special efforts to develop domestic industry in recent years. For example, the Norwegian Parliament approved the issuance of 500,000 Kronor in bonds to build the first domestic artificial fiber factory, and also approved the issuance of 400,000 Kronor in bonds to build the first copper factory; For example, the large number of small-scale Swedish sales products and grocery factories that appeared, even in the second quarter of this year, there were already 288 newly established joint-stock companies, with a total capital of 23 million Kronor. At the end of July, it also partnered with a Swiss textile factory to start building a raw silk spinning factory that can accommodate 120 looms; such as Finland's plan to separately build artificial fiber factories with annual outputs of 10,000 tons and 15,000 tons; all of these are concrete manifestations of these three countries' efforts to develop their domestic industry.

Due to the development of domestic industry, the industrial production index of the four Nordic countries has naturally also shown an increasing trend. If 1930 is taken as the benchmark, then at the end of June this year, the production index of the four Nordic countries was 120 percent, which is also an increase of six points compared to 114 percent at the end of June last year. Among them, the increase in production in the textile industry and the metal industry is the most significant. The following table shows the production index situation of the three Nordic countries except Denmark!

Sweden (1929 = 100)

End of May this year Same period last year

Total Index 109 101

Export Industry 87 80

Domestic Industry 121 112

Norway (First half of 1933 = 100)

End of May this year Same period last year

Total Index 111 105

Export Industry 109 96

Domestic Industry 113 110

Finland (1926 = 100)

End of March this year Same period last year

Export Industry 141 133

Domestic Industry 138 122

From this table, it can be seen that the industrial production of the Nordic countries has indeed shown signs of improvement. However, the main reason for this improvement is that the rationalization of production is artificially implemented and the exploitation of workers is intensified; it is not due to natural economic development. In fact, although the production index of the Nordic countries is on the rise, the lives of ordinary workers have not improved, and the number of unemployed has not decreased in proportion to the increase in production. For example, the number of unemployed people in Sweden, from the end of May last year to the end of May this year, only decreased from 14% of the total number of people with unemployment insurance to 10.5%; in Finland, the number of unemployed people in the same period

Continued from page 5

Page 26

Page 27

The number has only decreased from 24,000 to 13,000; the comparison between the number of unemployed people in Denmark and the total number of people registered for unemployment relief has decreased from 14% in July last year to 12.7% in July this year; and in Norway, the number of unemployed people has only decreased by 0.7% in one year since July last year.

As for the situation in the financial sector of the Nordic countries, there is no major change. Naturally, the phenomenon of strong demand for funds is also reflected in the assets of financial institutions, such as the increase in investment. However, most of the funds come directly from export profits, and the increase in bank investment is very small. At the same time, on the other hand, the increase in deposits is also very small, because its national income is dedicated to direct consumption, because of the use of credit unions and small-scale financial institutions in the Nordic countries.

However, the most noteworthy thing is the deterioration of Denmark's foreign capital calculation. Except for Denmark, the foreign exchange reserves of the three Nordic countries have increased, and there is no particular anxiety in terms of currency. However, the foreign debt of the National Bank of Denmark has increased from 81 million Kronor at the end of last year to 100 million Kronor at the end of July this year. This significant increase in foreign debt is mainly due to the sluggish export of agricultural products, the amount of decrease of which has reached 20 million Kronor in the first half of this year.

The above is a general overview of the recent economic situation in the Nordic countries. Generally speaking, although we can say that the recent economic situation in the Nordic countries has shown signs of improvement, whether this phenomenon can continue is still a question. Moreover, the four Nordic countries are not major capitalist countries. Therefore, their artificial, temporary, and partial economic improvement is of little significance in the midst of the ongoing economic panic in the entire capitalist world.

Biography of Famous People

Master Wood Carver Morikawa Doen 230

— An Uncollected Work

Wood carving is different from wood engraving: wood carving can be said to be the art of the feudal era, while wood engraving can be said to be the art of the modern era; wood carving is three-dimensional, while wood engraving is two-dimensional and combines carving with painting, so wood engraving is generally called woodcut painting.

Originally, Chinese wood carving was very famous, and foreigners often talked about it, but in general, we rarely see anything discussing Chinese wood carving: this has to be said to be a regret.

Japan also has some famous wood carvers, and the one to be introduced here is Morikawa Doen, who is known as a master wood carver. Of course, comparing Morikawa Doen's works with the famous ancient Chinese wood carvings, his artistic skills may not necessarily evoke our surprise, but when studying Japanese wood carving, he is worthy of special attention.

In Japan, there was a rice merchant named Kiemon, who had a son nicknamed Tomokichi. Tomokichi was very studious in his youth and loved painting and carving. Whenever he had time, he was very interested in doing his carving work. This young man was the later famous wood carving genius Morikawa Doen.

Speaking of Morikawa Doen, almost all elementary school students in Japan know him; his fame in carving can be said to be the same as our Zhong Yao and Wang Xizhi's reputation for being proficient in calligraphy. At the age of thirteen, he formally began to study painting with a teacher. When he was eighteen in Nara, Shibata Zeshin happened to be traveling to Nara. So he went to ask for his guidance, but Shibata Zeshin said to him: "There are many ancient fine art sculptures in Nara, and your character is suitable for the study of sculpture." From then on, he devoted himself more to the study of sculpture.

Previously, there was a famous sculptor in Nara named Shoto. At this time, Doen could see many works of this famous painter, which enabled him to concentrate on studying sculpture and engage in the production of Nara dolls. Therefore, his works in middle age were quite similar to Shoto's knife techniques. However, Doen's works contain a realistic flavor and are full of life, which can be said to be one of his characteristics.

By old age, Doen's skills were of course more mature. During the Meiji era, his imitations of ancient works were called by the Japanese as unparalleled in the world.

Among Doen's works, the particularly famous ones include: products of the National Industrial Exhibition; Meiji 10th year, Ranling King, Deer

Meiji 14th year, Lighting Ghost

Meiji 23rd year, Smiling Mask, Mask

Products of the American Chicago World's Fair:

Meiji 25th year, Male and Female Deer

Other:

Meiji 10th year, Wooden Statue of Takenouchi no Sukune

Meiji 16th year, Tentōki of Yufuku Temple, Hōryū-ji

Dogū, Two-Year-Old Statue of Prince Shotoku of Gokuraku-ji, Kimpu

Gilt Sutra Box of Senji Temple

Meiji 18th year, Mino Woodcutter, Kozobe no Maro

Wooden Statue of Zenfusenba Teishi

Meiji 28th year, Nine-Faced Kannon of Hōryū-ji

Doen's imitations of antiques are extremely detailed and realistic, making it simply impossible to distinguish the original object from his work. For example, some enthusiasts in Nara placed his imitation of the five-story pagoda of Hōryū-ji, the dogū, together with the original object for identification, but no one could distinguish them.

It is said that Doen was very honest and gentle, and did not compete with others, so people liked him very much. In the family, he also got along well with his younger siblings. Because he was very superstitious, he often accompanied his younger siblings to worship the gods. He usually ate, played, and shared his joys and sorrows with his family. In Japanese society, seeing brothers getting along very well is generally called "Morikawa style," which shows his influence on people. His wife came from a family of officials and was good at waka poetry. She had a very harmonious relationship with him and helped him greatly in all aspects; her help was indeed very significant to his success.

Doen's health has always been very good, and he rarely got sick. However, like many artistic geniuses of the past, he had a not-so-good habit: he loved to drink. Whether it was morning or evening, he could not leave the wine glass. Whenever he went out and returned late at night, he was mostly very drunk. Wine and carving can be said to be the two major elements on which he relied for his life, and he could not do without them. Even when he was eating, he would put the work he was carving and the wine in front of him, drinking and watching. When he was happy, he would immediately carve a stroke, and then he would be happier than anything else.

July 15, Meiji 27th year, was the day this genius sculptor bid farewell to the world forever. At this time, he was seventy-five years old. Many of the works he made in his life are kept in Nara and Tokyo. Many of those in Nara are forgeries, and very few of those in Tokyo are his genuine works; after the Great Tokyo Earthquake, the impact was even greater, and it is even more difficult to see his real works. Now, his works are not easy to see in Japan, which is very precious.

Special Account

Overseas Chinese Around the World (15) 231

— Zhong Minyi

The status of overseas Chinese in Honolulu, both socially and economically, is fairly good. Among them, the most are Cantonese, most of whom are engaged in business and labor. There are lawyers and those serving in banks, but their number is small. Generally speaking, the life of overseas Chinese here is not bad, but under various restrictions, it is feared that it will be very difficult for overseas Chinese here to develop in the future.

In addition, in Oceania, such as Samoa and the Bismarck Archipelago, there are also about a thousand Chinese laborers each, mostly contract laborers.

8. The Future of Overseas Chinese

From the above situation of overseas Chinese around the world, we can say that the overseas Chinese around the world, whether in Southeast Asia or in Europe and the Americas, have shown a trend from prosperity to decline; if the current situation continues to develop, then the future of overseas Chinese is indeed very pessimistic.

In recent years, the reasons why overseas Chinese in various places have been excluded everywhere and have increasingly shown a situation of decline are nothing more than these points: 1. The development of the power of overseas Chinese has aroused the jealousy of local people; 2. The development of the world economic panic has made the industry and commerce in various places depressed and the number of unemployed people has increased. Therefore, in the competition of industry and commerce, in the struggle for jobs, overseas Chinese have suffered great exclusion and restrictions; 3. Our national strength is not as good as others, and we cannot deal with the oppression and abuse suffered by overseas Chinese in various places with effective methods. Therefore, the authorities in various parts of the world can arbitrarily exclude, restrict, and oppress overseas Chinese. (To be continued)

Publishing World 234

The long-promoted masterpiece of the famous cartoonist Zhang Hongfei, the purely humorous "Zhang Mulang" pictorial, will be published on the first of next month. It is said that the style of the magazine is exquisite, with a color cover, a total of eight thick pages, finely printed on heavy Swedish newspaper, which is extremely valuable. Its humor is enough to surpass George Bernard Shaw, and the pictures are comparable to those of the American Haenigsen. It is a rare glorious harvest in the cartoon world in 1935. The price is six yuan, but for the sake of popular purchase, it is specially priced at only fifteen cents. Major bookstores and magazine companies have it for sale. It is said that the magazine is published by the Dazhong Comic Society.

Talking About Hu Ping's Acting Skills 235

— White Wood

"Hu Ping's acting skills in 'The Beginning of a Person' have indeed improved a lot." - This is the general consensus, and I am not just blindly praising her.

In fact, Hu Ping's acting skills are indeed improving day by day, and each play is better than the last. This is certainly due to the increase in experience, but mainly due to her willingness to work hard. Therefore, it is said: "Nothing is difficult in the world, as long as you have the will." Hu Ping is the most appropriate example.

Now, her new work "Hero of the Times" is about to meet the audience. She plays a "beauty" in the play, a romantic socialite. Because the personality is suitable, coupled with the usual willingness to work hard, she obviously has a very pleasant harvest. However, what must be specially mentioned here is her pure Mandarin and accurate pronunciation. Every word is pronounced very clearly, and the pitch of the voice is also very detailed. Therefore, in "Hero of the Times," not only has her acting skills made further progress, but also her lines have achieved extremely satisfactory success. So it can be said: "Hu Ping is indeed a rare and excellent sound film actress."

Tragic Scenes in "Parents and Children" 236

Floods, droughts... continuous natural and man-made disasters are tormenting China, which is in deep water.

The Cultural Film Company's "Parents and Children" takes the tragic and heartbreaking natural and man-made disasters as the background.

Under the scorching sun, in the barren fields, a tragedy of human hell unfolded: - A large group of unkempt refugees, men, women, old and young, don't know how many. Some of them have lost their parents, and some have lost their children. They have all been ruined by natural and man-made disasters. Now they are all struggling on the line of death due to hunger and cold, tears flowing from their bloodshot eyes. There are also many white-haired old men and infants in swaddling clothes, all groaning in human hell. Li Junpan, Xi Qiuxia, Hu Yichun, and Wu Yin also play the parents and children of a disaster-stricken family in Peidong Township..." Two cameras kept rolling, and tragic pictures of refugees were captured on camera. Therefore, the village scenes of "Parents and Children" are wailing ghosts and gods, shocking the world, and the content of "Parents and Children" is tragic, moving, and worthy of singing and crying.

The Cultural Company's location shooting team finished this scene of human hell and returned singing the "Parents and Children" song.
